[fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

[fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

[fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

## Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

## Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

## Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

## Project Scope

This page captures the Fordham Road bus-priority project as it moved from early feedback gathering into a preferred design direction. In June 2021, NYC DOT framed Fordham Road as one of the Bronx corridors identified for Better Buses priority treatments and used the public workshop to gather detailed feedback before presenting alternatives. [fordham_rd_major_deegan_expwy_boston_rd_jun2021#p004_c0003] [fordham_rd_major_deegan_expwy_boston_rd_jun2021#p014_c0003] By June 2023, the same project family was presented as Fordham Road - Inwood Bus Priority to Bronx Community Boards 11 and 5. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p001_c0001] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p001_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb5_jun2023#p001_c0002]

The need case combines bus ridership, equity, safety, and curb management. The 2021 workshop described 93,700 average daily riders on nine Fordham Road routes, including 40,300 on the Bx12 SBS and Local, while the 2023 deck emphasized 85,000 average daily bus riders on five routes and the Bx12 as the Bronx's busiest route. [fordham_rd_major_deegan_expwy_boston_rd_jun2021#p028_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p004_c0002] The same 2023 materials identify Fordham Road as a Vision Zero Priority Corridor with four priority intersections and 83 people killed or seriously injured between Deegan and Boston Road from 2014 to 2018. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p004_c0005]

## Existing Conditions

Before the proposed redesign, Fordham Road's bus priority was mostly curbside bus lanes, often with peak-period rules and a midday delivery window. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p005_c0002] DOT said the curbside lanes were frequently blocked throughout the day, forcing buses to weave into general traffic and making the existing condition poor for both bus passengers and other street users. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p006_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p009_c0002] The project materials also say bus speeds and ridership improved after the 2008 SBS launch but declined in later years, with the slowest Bx12-SBS segments westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p007_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p008_c0004]

## Outreach And Evaluation

The 2021 workshop was explicitly pre-design: DOT said it did not yet have a proposed design and would show alternatives after feedback and data analysis. [fordham_rd_major_deegan_expwy_boston_rd_jun2021#p021_c0002] The 2023 decks list a long outreach trail, including CAB meetings, merchant and shopper surveys, public polling, stakeholder briefings, a street intercept survey, and community-board presentations. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p012_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p012_c0004]

After the March 2022 CAB meeting, DOT says the project was put on hold while agencies ran a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, surveyed Arthur Avenue shoppers, and continued stakeholder discussions. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p013_c0005] ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022; the June 2023 materials report nearly 16,000 Fordham Road tickets through April 21, 2023 and a 4.7% April 2023 speed increase, but conclude enforcement alone had not restored prior bus speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p016_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p016_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p017_c0002]

## Alternatives And Preferred Direction

The June 2023 materials kept three alternatives in the record: Alternative A would convert and extend curbside bus lanes into 24/7 offset bus lanes; Alternative B would create an eastbound busway from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue, with westbound offset lanes; and Alternative C would create a two-way busway between Jerome and Webster Avenues. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p010_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p010_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p010_c0007] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p010_c0009]

DOT's traffic analysis counted traffic and pedestrians at more than 60 intersections, used anonymized GPS data for origin-destination analysis, modeled intersections, and tested scenarios from no volume reduction up to 40%. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p019_c0002] The reported model results for the three alternatives assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, shift modes, or use roadways outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p020_c0003]

By the CB11 and CB5 June 2023 presentations, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A. The stated rationale was that offset bus lanes best balanced bus speed, reliability, curb demand, and impacts on north-south bus corridors; the design was expected to add about 150 parking/loading spaces, while still acknowledging that double parking could block offset lanes. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p025_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb5_jun2023#p040_c0002] The next steps in the source-time plan were June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p026_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p026_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb11_jun2023#p026_c0005]
